Example 19 (Line 121):
Human Query: &gt; There was just a republican state that made it mandatory for teachers to disclose trans individuals to their families. 

There is no right for minors of any type to have the government hide things from their parents, though. Parents expect schools to inform them if their kids get into fights, cut classes, are diagnosed with a disease, are showing signs of suicidality, etc. And the state expects schools to inform the police of students show signs of abuse, etc.

Legally, schools act *in loco parentis* and minors in schools have no expectation or right to privacy with regard to schools hiding things from parents.

So this doesn't violate trans children's rights. They have no such right to violate, same as other children.

&gt; <Organization> are trying to ban things like hormone blockers for teens and other things that make it harder for people to transition.

No one im America has any right to any medical treatment whatsoever, except seriously injured people who make it to an ER -- they can't legally be pushed into the street and abandoned by the hospital. 

And no one has a right to any specific treatment -- if you want viagra and the doctors tell you no, for whatever reason, your rights have not been violated.

So this does not violate trans rights, either.

&gt; There‚Äôs a reason why trans people face such high suicide rates and it‚Äôs from an uncaring and hateful attitude perpetuated against them.

81% of transgender people have one or more personality disorders, with NPD being number one at 57%. This likely explains most trans suicide attempts. Many groups face an uncaring and hateful world and it's rare for more than a token few members to commit suicide. Blacks are a good example. Jews are an even better one -- violently hated by the entirety of <Organization> German society, persecuted, expropriated, regularly beaten and terrorised, and then sent off to slave labor and/or extermination camps, yet their suicide rate barely rose.

External factors do not account for the trans suicide rate. Which, by the way, is not much higher than the non-trans rate in adolescents.

Example 195 (Line 568):
Human Query: Frankly, speaking as a feminist, I'm mostly in agreement with you. Reproductive rights are important across the board, and men should have a fair deal of choice when it comes to it.

However, I still want to introduce some nuance here.

* There's a pragmatic concern here related to the welfare of the child. We don't want mothers and children living in poverty, and that has historically been a widespread problem that carries other social ills. Child support was invented as a measure not to say "punish" men, but rather to ensure that children were at least fed, clothed, housed and educated to prevent the suffering and social problems associated to lacking these things in early childhood. 

* As a corollary, I would require the introduction of robust child welfare programs to guarantee that, absent child support, the child will still have chances to do well and the mother won't fall into poverty. This includes things like free childcare programs, food assistance, and programs not unlike the Finnish baby boxes. I would still make these available to couples raising children together, though.

* Like you said, it is important that all parental rights be abdicated in cases that the father wishes to abstain from child support. It is also important that the father be "duly notified" of the pregnancy. I think the mother would have to demonstrate clear attempts to contact and notify the father within some specified timeframe. 

* Like you also kind of said, in many ways, raising a child is more onerous than a pay cut, in that it involves a lot of unpaid, thankless labor. This in itself creates an asymmetrical relationship between the burdens placed on each parent, and this in turn has to be considered when trying cases related to "financial abportion". This is why forcing women to "take responsibility" for an accident is placing a much greater burden on them than child support would be. <Person> broadly, I agree with you that options for men should exist, but you are obscuring the asymmetrical nature of the issue.
